    IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA 
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION 
CIVIL APPEAL NO.        OF 2026  
(ARISING OUT OF SLP (C) NO.6383 OF 2026) 
 
SMT. SHYAM KALI & ANR.               ...APPELLANT(S) 
 
VERSUS 
 
VIKAS VEER RASTOGI & ORS.            ...RESPONDENT(S)                                                                    
 
 
 O R D E R 
Leave granted. 
2. In a petition filed under the provisions of the 
Motor Vehicles Act, 1988 , the Motor Accident Claims 
Tribunal, Fatehpur, by award dated 20.07.2004 in 
M.A.C.P. Nos. 96 of 1999 and 199 of 2000, awarded 
compensation to the claimants in the following terms: 
“Both the petitions are allowed partly against the 
United India Insurance Company and the insurance 
company may recover the amount from the owner, 
according to law, as the owner has failed to 
discharge the burden of as mentioned in the body of 
judgment, for the compensation of Rs. 175000 (Rupees 
one lac seventy five thousand only) with interest at 
the rate of 6% annual from the date of judgement if 
the amount claimed is not deposited by the insurance 

## Page 11

2 
 
company within two months.  The petitioner no. 1 
Smt. Shyam Kali the widow of deceased will get Rs. 
65000/- (Rupees sixty five thousand) and rest of the 
petitioner s Km. Suman and Km. Sunita will get equal 
share of Rs. 55000/ -.  The share of the minor 
claimants has to be deposited in the fixed deposit 
scheme in the Nationalized Bank according to law, 
till date of their marriage.  The parties shall bear 
their own costs.” 
 
3. The aforesaid amount stood enhanced by the Hon’ble 
High Court of Judicature at Allahabad vide judgment 
dated 23.07.2019 in FAFO No. 2899 of 2004, whereby the 
compensation was reassessed at ₹4,00,000/ -, with the 
rate of interest enhanced from 6% to 9%. The operative 
portion of the High Court’s order reads as under: 
“The claimants are entitled to a total sum 
of ₹22,500 x 16 + 40,000 = ₹4,00,000/-. The 
amount shall carry interest at the rate of 
9% from the date of filing of the claim 
petition till award and 6% thereafter till 
deposit.”  
 
 
4. Having heard learned counsel for the parties, we 
are of the considered view that in the interest of 
justice, further enhancement of compensation is 
warranted.  
5. The deceased, Ram Kishore , aged about 35 years, 
lost his life in a motor accident on 11.03.1999. His 

## Page 12

3 
 
dependants, being his wife and daughters, are seeking 
just recompense. 
 Taking a holistic view of the matter, we direct 
that an additional sum of ₹2,00,000/- (Rupees Two Lakhs 
only) be awarded as lump -sum compensation, over and 
above what has already been granted by the Tribunal and 
the High Court.  Ordered accordingly. 
6. Accordingly, the total compensation payable to the 
claimants shall stand modified as directed by the High 
Court.  
7. The liability to satisfy the award shall remain 
upon the insurer, i.e., Respondent No. 2. The amount 
be directly remitted into the bank account of the 
claimants. The particulars of the bank account are to 
be immediately supplied by the learned counsel for the 
appellants to the learned counsel for the respondent. 
The amount be remitted positively within a period of 
eight weeks thereafter.  
8. The impugned judgment of the High Court stands 
modified to the above extent. 
 

## Page 13

4 
 
9. The appeal is accordingly allowed in part.

38377/2025 passed by the High Court of Madhya Pradesh
Principal Seat at Jabalpur granted to respondent no.2
namely  Kamta  Bhushan  Pandey  who  was  released  on

## Page 22

anticipatory bail.
2. After hearing learned counsel for the parties, it is
true that the order impugned is unreasoned. But in any
case, at present, respondent no.2 has been released on
anticipatory bail since last about more than 08 months and
chargesheet has been filed in the meantime.  The charges
have already been framed and the trial is in progress,
however, without going into the merits setting aside of
the order at this stage is not desirable.
3. As such, we are not inclined to interfere in this
Special  Leave  Petition.  It  is  suffice  to  say  that
respondent no.2 ought to regularly appear before the
concerned Trial Court and shall not ask any unnecessary
adjournment during the trial. He shall not intimidate any
of the witnesses. Otherwise, in default the Petitioner is
at is at liberty to approach the Court concerned for
cancellation of bail of respondent no.2.
4. With  the  above  observations,  the  Special  Leave
Petition is disposed of.

disposed of.

Date : 29-05-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :

         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE S.V.N. BHATTI
For Petitioner(s) : 
                   Ms. Vanshaja Shukla, Adv.

                   Ms. C. Ankeeta Appanna, AOR

For Respondent(s) :

                   Mr. Ajay Sharma, Adv.
                   Mr. Rahul Sharma, Adv.
                   Ms. Laksheka Garg, Adv.                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Exemption Application is allowed.
2. We heard Ms. Vanshaja Shukla, the learned counsel appearing
for the petitioner and Ms. Malvika Trivedi, the  learned Senior
counsel appearing for the respondent.

## Page 28

2
3. We take notice of the fact that both the parties are Micro,
Small and Medium Enterprises (MSME). The respondent is the original
claimant. 
4. There are two Awards before us.
5. The operative part of the first Award reads thus:- 
I. The Claimant is entitled to get an amount of Rs.23,26,284/-
being the principal outstanding amount from the respondent;
II. The Claimant is also entitled to receive interest as per
provisions of Section 16 of MSMED Act, 2006 from the appointed
day or the agreed day of respective invoice till the actual
payment from the respondents;
III. The Claimant is entitled to get sum of Rs. 60,000/- as
arbitration  fees  and  towards  litigation  expenses  from  the
respondent side as mentioned in the report of the empanelled
expert  in  terms  of  section  31(A)  of  the  Arbitration  and
Conciliation Act, 1996.
IV. The Claimant is entitled to receive a sum of Rs. 3,500/- from
the  respondent  as  processing  fee  and  the  claimant  is  also
entitled for Rs. 2,500/- which he has assured to deposit in favor
of the Council on behalf of the respondent as processing fee.
6.  The operative part of Second Award reads thus:-
I. The Claimant is entitled to get an amount of Rs.30,30,932/-
being the principal outstanding amount from the respondent
II. The Claimant is also entitled to receive interest as per
provisions of Section 16 of MSMED Act, 2006 from the appointed
day or the agreed day of respective invoice till the actual
payment from the respondents.
III. The Claimant is entitled to get sum of Rs. 60,000/- as
arbitration  fees  and  towards  litigation  expenses  from  the
respondent side as mentioned in the report of the empanelled
expert  in  terms  of  section  31(A)  of  the  Arbitration  and
Conciliation Act, 1996.
IV. The Claimant is entitled to receive a sum of Rs. 3,500/- from
the  respondent  as  processing  fee  and  the  claimant  is  also
entitled for Rs. 2,500/- which he has assured to deposit in favor
of the Council on behalf of the respondent as processing fee.
7. After the Awards came to be passed, the respondent went for
execution of the same. In the execution proceedings, objections
were raised by the petitioner which came to be overruled.
8. Being dissatisfied with the same, the petitioner went before
the High Court invoking supervisory jurisdiction under Article 227

## Page 29

3
of the Constitution.
9. The High Court declined to interfere and rejected both the
revision petitions.
10. Two contentions have been raised before us by the learned
counsel appearing for the petitioner. First with regard to the
applicability of Section 29A of the Arbitration and Conciliation
Act, 1996 and secondly as regards Section 18(3) of the MSME Act,
2006.
11. We  are  further  informed  that  the  bank  accounts  of  the
petitioner are already under attachment.
12. On the other hand, the learned Senior counsel appearing for
the Respondent submitted that no error not to speak of any error of
law could be said to have been committed by the High Court in
declining to entertain the two Revision Petitions in exercise of
its Supervisory Jurisdiction under Article 227 of the constitution.
She would submit that instead of invoking Section 34 of the
Arbitration Act for the purpose of challenging the two awards, the
petitioner went before the High Court invoking its supervisory
jurisdiction. She would further submit that insofar as Section 18
(3) of the MSME Act is concerned, it has been held to be directory
and so far as Section 29A of the Arbitration Act is concerned, the
High Court has dealt with this contention in details relying upon
few decisions.
13. Issue notice, returnable on 15-7-2026. 
14. Ms. Mahak Rathee, the learned Advocate-on-Record accepts and
waives formal notice for and on behalf of the sole respondent.

## Page 31

Mr. Yashraj Singh Bundela, AOR
Ms. Pratima Singh, Adv.
Mr. Arpit Garg, Adv. 
                   
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
SLP(Crl) No. 17001/2025
1. The submission of the learned counsel for the
petitioner is that the First Information Report (“FIR”)
had indicted the concerned respondent as one of the
perpetrators of the crime and the testimony of the eye-
witness confirmed the same and, therefore, the Trial
Court invoked its powers under Section 319 of the Code
of Criminal Procedure, 1973 (“CrPC”) to summon the
second respondent. It is submitted that the High Court
erred in law by interferring with Trial Court’s order
by taking into consideration the defence plea of alibi.
It is submitted that the defence plea of alibi is to be
considered in trial and not at the stage of considering
an application for arraigning an accused under Section
319 Cr.PC.
2. Reliance has been placed on a decision of this
Court in Harjinder Singh Vs. The State of Punjab and
Anr.1 to canvass that plea of alibi is not to be taken
into consideration for rejecting an application under
Section 319 Cr.PC particularly where the allegations
1 2025 INSC 634
2

## Page 32

against the proposed accused are there in the FIR and
the testimony recorded in the course of the trial.
3. Issue notice, returnable on 28.07.2026.
4. Notice on behalf of the respondent has been
accepted by Mr Yashraj Singh Bundela, AOR.
5. In the meantime the effect and operation of the
impugned order dated 17.08.2026 passed by the High
Court shall remain stayed.
SLP(Crl) No. 17019/2025
Issue notice, returnable on 28.07.2026.
  (PRIYANKA MALIK)                              (SAPNA BANSAL)
SENIOR PERSONAL ASSISTANT                     COURT MASTER (NSH)

SLP(C)No. 16483/2023:
1. Learned counsel for the petitioners submitted that the
first petitioner has died. Hence, an application for
substitution has been filed.
2. There being no objection to the said application, the
application for substitution is allowed.
3. The  proposed  legal  representatives  of  deceased
petitioner No.1 are ordered to be brought on record as
legal representatives of deceased petitioner.
4. Petitioners’ counsel to file amended memo of parties.
Diary No(s). 31179/2024:
1. Learned counsel for respondent No.1 submitted that
respondent No.1 has died.
2. Learned counsel for respondent No.1 submitted that
instead  of  filing  an  impleadment  application,  an
application  for  substitution  of  the  legal
representatives of respondent No.1 has been filed. The
same may be considered as an impleading application
and may be allowed.
3. There  being  no  objection  on  the  side  of  the
petitioner(s) to the said application, the application
for substitution is allowed.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
MISCELLANEOUS APPLICATION NO.             OF 2025
(DIARY NO.29624 OF 2026)
IN
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO. 413 OF 2025
IVAN RATHINAM APPELLANT(S)/
APPLICANT(S)
VERSUS
MILAN JOSEPH RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Delay condoned.
2. The instant application has been filed seeking the following
relief(s):
“(a)  Allow the present application and pass a direction
to Internet platforms like Indian Kanoon and Google to
redact the petitioner’s names from the orders/judgments
accessible online;
(b) Pass such other further orders, as this Hon’ble
Court  may  deem  fit  and  proper  in  the  facts  and
circumstances of this case.”
3. It is pertinent to note that there have been multiple rounds
of litigation between the parties, including before the Civil
Courts and the Family Court. It appears to us that the relief
sought  presently  will  have  to  be  granted  qua the  earlier
judgements/orders  given  by  these  Courts  as  well.  In  such
circumstances, the effective recourse for the applicant would be to
approach the High Court through appropriate proceedings.
4. The  application  (IA  No.150474/2026)  and  miscellaneous
application are, accordingly, disposed of with liberty to the
applicant  to  approach  the  High  Court  through  appropriate
1

## Page 82

proceedings. In case the High Court accepts the applicant’s claim,
the same shall  ipso facto  apply to Criminal Appeal No.413/2025,
which was decided by this Court vide judgment dated 28.01.2025.
..........................CJI.
       (SURYA KANT)
..........................J.
       (JOYMALYA BAGCHI)
           
NEW DELHI;
MAY 26, 2026

## Page 84

ITEM NO.14               COURT NO.1               SECTION IX
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (C)  No(s).  18274/2026
[Arising out of impugned judgment and order dated 01-04-2026 in WPL
No. 39995/2025 passed by the High Court of Judicature at Bombay]
AJAYKUMAR SHYAMKISHOR TRIPATHI & ORS.              Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
REGISTRAR GENERAL & ANR.                           Respondent(s)
Date : 26-05-2026 This petition was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE THE CHIEF JUSTICE
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Prashant Bhushan, Adv.
                   Mr. Niraj Gupta, AOR
                   Mrs. Anshu Gupta, Adv.
                   Mr. Subham Gupta, Adv.
                   Ms. Siddhi Gupta, Adv.
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The petitioners in this Special Leave Petition are advocates
practicing in various courts in the State of Maharashtra. They
appeared in the 2024 Selection Process for recruitment to the post
of  District  Judges,  namely,  the  Maharashtra  Higher  Judicial
Services. The selection process comprised two parts, i.e. the
written  examination  and  the  viva  voce.  The  petitioners  have
apparently performed well in the written examination, with one of
them, statedly, having secured the third-highest marks in it.
Initially,  28  posts  were  advertised,  but  subsequently,  more
vacancies became available, which were added through two addenda,
1

## Page 85

resulting in a total of 42 vacant posts. Having cleared the written
examination,  the  petitioners  were  called  for  the  viva  voce.
However, they failed to secure more than 40% i.e., 20 marks,
prescribed as the qualifying marks. As a result of this, their
names did not feature in the final selection list. Ultimately, the
High Court was able to select only 13 candidates against 42
vacancies. Aggrieved by the non-inclusion of their names in the
final selection list, the unsuccessful petitioners approached the
High Court, but their writ petition was dismissed, giving rise to
the instant proceedings.  
2. We have heard Mr. Prashant Bhushan, learned counsel for the
petitioners and perused the record. Various issues, such as the
prescription of minimum marks for viva voce and/or uniformity in
the prescription of such marks on a pan-India basis, have been
raised during the course of arguments. However, we are of the view
that such issues may be independently examined by this Court in the
proceedings already pending before us concerning the judicial
services.
3. As regards the petitioners, it is evident that they could not
be selected only owing to their inability to secure the minimum
qualifying marks in the viva voce. Since large-scale vacancies have
remained unfilled, and two out of three of the petitioners are
women  candidates,  with  one  belonging  to  the  Scheduled  Caste
category, it seems to us that the petitioners’ candidature can be
sympathetically reconsidered by the High Court. In this regard, if
the High Court is satisfied, the requirement of minimum marks for
viva voce may be relaxed by invoking the appropriate powers under
2

## Page 86

the statutory rules and/or the High Court may invoke any other
mechanism to facilitate such reconsideration. We, however, leave it
to the complete discretion of the High Court to adjudge the overall
suitability of the petitioners. All that we observe is that,
keeping in view the fact that a substantial part of the vacancies
remained  unfilled,  the  claim  of  the  petitioners  may  be
sympathetically reconsidered.
4. The Special Leave Petition is disposed of accordingly.
5. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand closed.  
(NITIN TALREJA)                              (PREETHI DILEEP KUMAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                        ASSISTANT REGISTRAR
3

## Page 87

1. Exemption Application is allowed.
2. The total amount due and payable by the petitioners to the
Bank is Rs.47,42,531/- (Rupees Forty Seven Lakh, Forty Two Thousand
Five Hundred and Thirty One)
3. Ms. Anitha Shenoy, the learned Senior counsel appearing for
the petitioners would submit that Rs.10,00,000/- (Rupees Ten Lakh)
has already been deposited by her clients, however, the same has
not been credited in the loan account. She  has  instructions  from
her clients to make a Statement that Rs.10,00,000/- would be

## Page 120

2
deposited within a period of 2 days from today with the Bank in
addition to Rs.10,00,000/- which has already been deposited and the
balance amount of Rs. 27,42,531/- (Rupees Twenty Seven Lakh, Forty
Two Thousand, Five Hundred and Thirty One) would be deposited on or
before 22nd June, 2026 as fixed by the High Court for further
hearing of the Writ Petition.
4. Since the petitioners have expressed their willingness to
deposit the amount, we are inclined to issue notice and order that
status-quo be maintained, returnable on 28-7-2026. 
5. We make ourselves very clear that insofar as the impugned
Order is concerned, we find no error in the same. The petitioners
have no case on merits. However, since the entire dwelling unit is
at stake and the petitioners are ready and willing to deposit this
amount, we have shown this indulgence.

          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. This petition emanates from proceedings under
Section 28 of the U.P. Land Revenue Act, 1901 relating
to  correction  of  maps.  It  is  well-settled  that
proceedings under Section 28 are summary in nature
1

## Page 130

which are subject to regular suit proceedings. In such
circumstances, if the petitioner is aggrieved by any
order of correction of the maps, he can take recourse
to an appropriate remedy either before the Revenue
Court or Civil Court as may be advised.
2. With the aforesaid liberty, the Special Leave
Petition stands disposed of.
3. Pending  application(s),  if  any,  shall  stand
disposed of.

stated that the High Court is reopening after summer
vacation on 15.06.2026 and no date has been fixed by
the High Court for considering the matter.
4. If the petitioner herein seeks vacating of the interim
order granted by the High Court, the same shall be
considered in the first instance and the main matter
could be disposed of. The High Court shall consider the
said  request  as  expeditiously  as  possible  and  in
accordance with law.
5. We  say  so  for  the  reason  that  the  respondents-
authorities have understood the impugned order to mean
a stay of investigation.
6. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed
of.
(RADHA SHARMA)                                  (DIVYA BABBAR)

ITEM NO.41               COURT NO.1               SECTION X
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Writ Petition(s)(Criminal)  No(s).  193/2026
AMARDEEP KUMAR                                     Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF DELHI NCT & ORS.                      Respondent(s)
IA No. 153433/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 25-05-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE THE CHIEF JUSTICE
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Jay Savla, Sr. Adv.
                   Mr. Jaspreet Singh Rai, Adv.
                   Mr. Rohit Nagpal, Adv.
                   Mrs. Sukhdeep Kaur Rai, Adv.
                   Mr. Ankur Singh, Adv.
                   Ms. Apoorvapal, Adv.
                   Mr. Shyamal Kumar, AOR
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. No case to entertain the instant writ petition or entrust the
investigation to CBI in terms of Section 30 of the Banning of
Unregulated Deposit Schemes Act, 2019, at the instance of the
petitioner, is made out.  
2. It may be noticed that the petitioner is the Managing Director
of M/s. Capital Protection Force Pvt. Ltd. The said company
commenced an invoice discounting business from 2020 under the name
‘Falcon  Invoice  Discounting’,  through  which  investments  were
invited from the public via an online platform. Investors were
1

## Page 182

offered returns based on the discounting of trade receivables and
invoices. The case against the petitioner are that the aforesaid
platform,  operating  across  multiple  States,  functioned  as  an
unregulated deposit scheme that collected money from the public
without adhering to applicable regulatory frameworks. There are
consequential allegations against the petitioner of duping the
innocent investors of their investments.
3. We have heard the learned senior counsel for the petitioner
with reference to the claim under Section 30 of the 2019 Act. In
our considered opinion, the said Act does not grant the accused an
enforceable right to seek transfer of FIR for investigation to the
CBI. Such a recourse, though, may be permitted to be availed by the
victims of the crimes. 
4. The Writ Petition is, accordingly, dismissed.
5. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand closed.
(NITIN TALREJA)                              (PREETHI DILEEP KUMAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                        ASSISTANT REGISTRAR
2

ITEM NO.53               COURT NO.1               SECTION X
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Writ Petition(s)(Criminal)  No(s).  215/2026
AMARENDRA KUMAR PANDEY @ PAPPU PANDEY & ANR.       Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF BIHAR & ORS.                          Respondent(s)
(IA No. 166982/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.)
 
Date : 27-05-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE THE CHIEF JUSTICE
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. Manan Kumar Mishra, Sr. Adv.
                   Ms. Anjul Dwivedi, Adv.
                   Mr. Saurabh Tiwari, Adv.
                   Dr. Ram Sankar, Adv.
                   M/S. Ram Sankar & Co, AOR
                   
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The petitioners have approached this Court under Article 32 of
the Constitution seeking quashing of the criminal proceedings
arising  out  of  FIR  No.5139008260161  of  2026  registered  at
Kuchaikote P.S., District Gopalganj.  The aforesaid case has been
registered under Sections 329(3), 308(4), 308(5), 352, 109(1),
3(5), 111(3) and (4) of the Bharatiya Nyaya Sanhita (BNS) 2023 and
Section 27 of the Arms Act, 1959.
2. Petitioner No.1 is a sitting member of the Bihar State
Legislative  Assembly,  who  has  been  elected  six  times,  and
Petitioner No.2 is his elder brother. It seems that there is a
title dispute between the petitioners and family members on the one
1

## Page 190

hand and the private respondents on the other hand. With respect to
such a dispute, Title Suit Nos. 255 of 2024 and 662 of 2024 are
said to be pending before the Civil Court. The case of the
petitioners is that the subject land was purchased by their father
way  back  in  September  1978  through  a  registered  sale  deed.
However, the subject cases have now been registered, alleging
various offences purportedly committed by them.  
3. It is, however, fairly admitted by learned senior counsel for
the petitioners that a quashing petition filed by the petitioners
is pending before the Patna High Court. There being a summer
vacation, the petitioners apprehend coercive action at the hands of
the Police even though their quashing petition is pending before
the High Court.  
4. Taking into consideration all the attending circumstances and
without expressing any opinion on merits, it is directed that no
coercive action shall be taken against the petitioners pursuant to
FIR No.5139008260161 of 2026 till the matter is taken up for
effective hearing by the High Court. Meanwhile, the petitioners are
directed to move an appropriate application before the High Court
for early disposal of their pending petition. We request the High
Court to prioritise the hearing in the matter and pass appropriate
orders.  However, it is clarified that we have not expressed any
opinion on the merits of the case.
5. The Writ Petition is disposed of with pending application(s),
if any.
(NITIN TALREJA)                              (PREETHI DILEEP KUMAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                        ASSISTANT REGISTRAR
2

1. After some arguments, learned counsel for the petitioner prays
to withdraw the Special Leave Petition by seeking liberty to apply
to the High court for expeditious disposal of the pending appeal
taking into account that petitioner has suffered incarceration of
about seven years.
2.  In view of the above, we deem it appropriate to dismiss the
petition as withdrawn with liberty as prayed for.
   
   (KAVITA PAHUJA)                             (SAPNA BANSAL)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                       COURT MASTER (NSH)
